<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Damage_to_human_health">Damage to human health<span id="Health_effects"></span></span></h2>
<p>The use of coal as fuel causes ill health and deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The deadly <a href="/wiki/Pea_soup_fog#London" title="Pea soup fog">London smog</a> was caused primarily by the heavy use of coal. Globally coal is estimated to cause 800,000 premature deaths every year,<sup id="cite_ref-Endcoal_health_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Endcoal_health-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> mostly in India<sup id="cite_ref-Economist2018_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2018-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and China.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Burning coal is a major emitter of <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>, which creates PM2.5 <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a>, the most dangerous form of air pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coal smokestack emissions cause <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strokes" class="mw-redirect" title="Strokes">strokes</a>, reduced <a href="/wiki/Intelligence" title="Intelligence">intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">artery</a> blockages, <a href="/wiki/Heart_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart attacks">heart attacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Congestive_heart_failure" class="mw-redirect" title="Congestive heart failure">congestive heart failure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrhythmias" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiac arrhythmias">cardiac arrhythmias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury poisoning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stenosis" title="Stenosis">arterial occlusion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">lung cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-psr_coal-damages-health_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psr_coal-damages-health-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Annual health costs in Europe from use of coal to generate electricity are estimated at up to €43 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In China, improvements to air quality and human health would increase with more stringent climate policies, mainly because the country's energy is so heavily reliant on coal. And there would be a net economic benefit.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2017 study in the <i>Economic Journal</i> found that for Britain during the period 1851–1860, "a one standard deviation increase in coal use raised infant mortality by 6–8% and that industrial coal use explains roughly one-third of the urban mortality penalty observed during this period."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Breathing in <a href="/wiki/Coal_dust" title="Coal dust">coal dust</a> causes <a href="/wiki/Coalworker%27s_pneumoconiosis" title="Coalworker&#39;s pneumoconiosis">coalworker's pneumoconiosis</a> which is known colloquially as "black lung", so-called because the coal dust literally turns the lungs black from their usual pink color.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In the United States alone, it is estimated that 1,500 former employees of the coal industry die every year from the effects of breathing in coal mine dust.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Huge amounts of coal ash and other waste is produced annually. Use of coal generates hundreds of millions of tons of ash and other waste products every year. These include <a href="/wiki/Fly_ash" title="Fly ash">fly ash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bottom_ash" title="Bottom ash">bottom ash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flue-gas_desulfurization" title="Flue-gas desulfurization">flue-gas desulfurization</a> sludge, that contain <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">heavy metals</a>, along with non-metals such as <a href="/wiki/Selenium" title="Selenium">selenium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Around 10% of coal is ash:<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coal_ash" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal ash">coal ash</a> is hazardous and toxic to human beings and some other living things.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Coal ash contains the radioactive elements <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>. Coal ash and other solid combustion byproducts are stored locally and escape in various ways that expose those living near coal plants to radiation and environmental toxics.<sup id="cite_ref-sa-coal-ash-more-rdactiv_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sa-coal-ash-more-rdactiv-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Damage_to_the_environment">Damage to the environment</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_the_coal_industry" title="Environmental impact of the coal industry">Environmental impact of the coal industry</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg/220px-Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg/330px-Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg/440px-Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="828" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photograph of the site of the <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Fossil_Plant" title="Kingston Fossil Plant">Kingston Fossil Plant</a> coal fly ash slurry spill taken the day after <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Fossil_Plant_coal_fly_ash_slurry_spill" title="Kingston Fossil Plant coal fly ash slurry spill">the event</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">Coal mining</a> and coal fueling of <a href="/wiki/Power_stations" class="mw-redirect" title="Power stations">power stations</a> and industrial processes can cause major environmental damage.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Water systems are affected by coal mining.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> For example, mining affects <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">water table</a> levels and acidity. Spills of fly ash, such as the <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Fossil_Plant_coal_fly_ash_slurry_spill" title="Kingston Fossil Plant coal fly ash slurry spill">Kingston Fossil Plant coal fly ash slurry spill</a>, can also contaminate land and waterways, and destroy homes. Power stations that burn coal also consume large quantities of water. This can affect the flows of rivers, and has consequential impacts on other land uses. In areas of <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">water scarcity</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Thar_Desert" title="Thar Desert">Thar Desert</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, coal mining and coal power plants would use significant quantities of water.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the earliest known impacts of coal on the <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle" title="Water cycle">water cycle</a> was <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>. Approximately 75 <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude_(mass)#106_to_1011_kg" title="Orders of magnitude (mass)">Tg</a>/S per year of <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> (SO<sub>2</sub>) is released from burning coal. After release, the sulfur dioxide is oxidized to gaseous H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>2</sub> which scatters solar radiation, hence its increase in the atmosphere exerts a cooling effect on climate. This beneficially masks some of the warming caused by increased greenhouse gases. However, the sulfur is precipitated out of the atmosphere as acid rain in a matter of weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> whereas carbon dioxide remains in the atmosphere for hundreds of years. Release of SO<sub>2</sub> also contributes to the widespread acidification of ecosystems.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Disused coal mines can also cause issues. Subsidence can occur above tunnels, causing damage to infrastructure or cropland. Coal mining can also cause long lasting fires, and it has been estimated that thousands of <a href="/wiki/Coal_seam_fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal seam fire">coal seam fires</a> are burning at any given time.<sup id="cite_ref-Deep_underground_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deep_underground-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Brennender_Berg" title="Brennender Berg">Brennender Berg</a> has been burning since 1668 and is still burning in the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-mineralienatlas_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mineralienatlas-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The production of coke from coal produces <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a>, coal tar, and gaseous compounds as by-products which if discharged to land, air or waterways can pollute the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Whyalla_steelworks" class="mw-redirect" title="Whyalla steelworks">Whyalla steelworks</a> is one example of a coke producing facility where liquid ammonia is discharged to the marine environment.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Underground_fires">Underground fires</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coal-seam_fire" title="Coal-seam fire">Coal-seam fire</a></div>
<p>Thousands of coal fires are burning around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Those burning underground can be difficult to locate and many cannot be extinguished. Fires can cause the ground above to subside, their combustion gases are dangerous to life, and breaking out to the surface can initiate surface <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">wildfires</a>. Coal seams can be set on fire by <a href="/wiki/Spontaneous_combustion" title="Spontaneous combustion">spontaneous combustion</a> or contact with a <a href="/wiki/Mine_fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Mine fire">mine fire</a> or surface fire. Lightning strikes are an important source of ignition. The coal continues to burn slowly back into the seam until oxygen (air) can no longer reach the flame front. A grass fire in a coal area can set dozens of coal seams on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Coal fires in China burn an estimated 120 million tons of coal a year, emitting 360 million metric tons of CO<sub>2</sub>, amounting to 2–3% of the annual worldwide production of CO<sub>2</sub> from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Centralia,_Pennsylvania" title="Centralia, Pennsylvania">Centralia, Pennsylvania</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Borough_(Pennsylvania)" title="Borough (Pennsylvania)">borough</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Coal_Region" title="Coal Region">Coal Region</a> of the United States), an exposed vein of anthracite ignited in 1962 due to a trash fire in the borough landfill, located in an abandoned <a href="/wiki/Anthracite_coal" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthracite coal">anthracite</a> <a href="/wiki/Surface_mining" title="Surface mining">strip mine</a> pit. Attempts to extinguish the fire were unsuccessful, and it <a href="/wiki/Centralia_mine_fire" title="Centralia mine fire">continues to burn underground to this day</a>. The Australian <a href="/wiki/Burning_Mountain" title="Burning Mountain">Burning Mountain</a> was originally believed to be a volcano, but the smoke and ash come from a coal fire that has been burning for some 6,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At Kuh i Malik in <a href="/wiki/Yagnob_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Yagnob Valley">Yagnob Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, coal deposits have been burning for thousands of years, creating vast underground labyrinths full of unique minerals, some of them very beautiful.
</p><p>The reddish siltstone rock that caps many ridges and buttes in the <a href="/wiki/Powder_River_Basin" title="Powder River Basin">Powder River Basin</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> and in western <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a> is called <i>porcelanite</i>, which resembles the coal burning waste "clinker" or volcanic "<a href="/wiki/Scoria" title="Scoria">scoria</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Clinker is rock that has been fused by the natural burning of coal. In the Powder River Basin approximately 27 to 54 billion tons of coal burned within the past three million years.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Wild coal fires in the area were reported by the <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Clark_Expedition" title="Lewis and Clark Expedition">Lewis and Clark Expedition</a> as well as explorers and settlers in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_warming">Global warming</span></h3>
<p>The largest and most long term effect of coal use is the release of carbon dioxide, a <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> that causes <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>. Coal-fired power plants were the single largest contributor to the growth in global CO<sub>2</sub> emissions in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-Gençsü_2019,_p._8_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gençsü_2019,_p._8-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> 40% of the total fossil fuel emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-phys2018_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phys2018-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Coal mining can emit methane, another greenhouse gas.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016 world gross <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon dioxide emissions">carbon dioxide emissions</a> from coal usage were 14.5 giga tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> For every megawatt-hour generated, coal-fired electric power generation emits around a tonne of carbon dioxide, which is double the approximately 500&#160;kg of carbon dioxide released by a <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>-fired electric plant.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the head of the UN climate agency advised that most of the world's coal reserves should be left in the ground to avoid catastrophic global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> To keep global warming below 1.5°C or 2°C hundreds, or possibly thousands, of coal-fired power plants will need to be retired early.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coal_pollution_mitigation">Coal pollution mitigation</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coal_pollution_mitigation" title="Coal pollution mitigation">Coal pollution mitigation</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Clean_coal_technology" title="Clean coal technology">Clean coal technology</a></div>
<p>"Clean" coal technology usually addresses atmospheric problems resulting from burning coal. Historically, the primary focus was on SO<sub>2</sub> and NO<sub>x</sub>, the most important gases which caused <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a> which cause visible air pollution, illness and premature deaths. SO<sub>2</sub> can be removed by <a href="/wiki/Flue-gas_desulfurization" title="Flue-gas desulfurization">flue-gas desulfurization</a> and NO<sub>2</sub> by <a href="/wiki/Selective_catalytic_reduction" title="Selective catalytic reduction">selective catalytic reduction</a> (SCR). Particulates can be removed with <a href="/wiki/Electrostatic_precipitator" title="Electrostatic precipitator">electrostatic precipitators</a>. Although perhaps less efficient <a href="/wiki/Wet_scrubber" title="Wet scrubber">wet scrubbers</a> can remove both gases and particulates. And <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a> emissions can be reduced up to 95%.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> However capturing carbon dioxide emissions is generally not economically viable.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Standards">Standards</span></h3>
<p>Local pollution standards include GB13223-2011 (China), India,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Emissions_Directive" title="Industrial Emissions Directive">Industrial Emissions Directive</a> (EU) and the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act (United States)</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_monitoring">Satellite monitoring</span></h3>
<p>Satellite monitoring is now used to crosscheck national data, for example <a href="/wiki/Sentinel-5_Precursor" title="Sentinel-5 Precursor">Sentinel-5 Precursor</a> has shown that Chinese control of SO<sub>2</sub> has only been partially successful.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> It has also revealed that low use of technology such as SCR has resulted in high NO<sub>2</sub> emissions in South Africa and India.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Combined_cycle_power_plants">Combined cycle power plants</span></h3>
<p>A few <a href="/wiki/Integrated_gasification_combined_cycle" title="Integrated gasification combined cycle">Integrated gasification combined cycle</a> (IGCC) coal-fired power plants have been built with <a href="/wiki/Coal_gasification" title="Coal gasification">coal gasification</a>. Although they burn coal more efficiently and therefore emit less pollution, the technology has not generally proved economically viable for coal, except possibly in Japan although this is controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbon_capture_and_storage">Carbon capture and storage</span></h3>
<p>Although still being intensively researched and considered economically viable for some uses other than with coal; <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">carbon capture and storage</a> has been tested at the <a href="/wiki/Petra_Nova" title="Petra Nova">Petra Nova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Dam_Power_Station" title="Boundary Dam Power Station">Boundary Dam</a> coal-fired power plants and has been found to be technically feasible but not economically viable for use with coal, due to reductions in the cost of solar PV technology.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span></h2>
<p>In 2018 USD 80 billion was invested in coal supply but almost all for sustaining production levels rather than opening new mines.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
In the long term coal and oil could cost the world trillions of dollars per year.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Coal alone may cost Australia billions,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> whereas costs to some smaller companies or cities could be on the scale of millions of dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The economies most damaged by coal (via climate change) may be India and the US as they are the countries with the highest <a href="/wiki/Social_cost_of_carbon" class="mw-redirect" title="Social cost of carbon">social cost of carbon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Bank loans to finance coal are a risk to the Indian economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist2018_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2018-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>China is the largest producer of coal in the world. It is the world's largest energy consumer, and <a href="/wiki/Coal_in_China" title="Coal in China">coal in China</a> supplies 60% of its primary energy. However two fifths of China's coal power stations are estimated to be loss-making.<sup id="cite_ref-CarbTrk2018_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarbTrk2018-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Air pollution from coal storage and handling costs the USA almost 200 dollars for every extra ton stored, due to PM2.5.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Coal pollution costs the EU €43 billion each year.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Measures to cut air pollution benefit individuals financially and the economies of countries<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> such as China.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidies">Subsidies</span></h3>
<p>Broadly defined total subsidies for coal in 2015 have been estimated at around US$2.5 trillion, about 3% of global <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Coal&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> countries provide at least  US$63.9 billion<sup id="cite_ref-Gençsü_2019,_p._8_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gençsü_2019,_p._8-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> of government support per year for the production of coal, including coal-fired power: many subsidies are impossible to quantify<sup id="cite_ref-ClimateTransparency2019_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ClimateTransparency2019-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> but they include US$27.6 billion in domestic and international public finance, US$15.4 billion in fiscal support, and US$20.9 billion in state-owned enterprise (SOE) investments per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Gençsü_2019,_p._8_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gençsü_2019,_p._8-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In the EU state aid to new coal-fired plants is banned from 2020, and to existing coal-fired plants from 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> However government funding for new coal power plants is being supplied via <a href="/wiki/Exim_Bank_of_China" title="Exim Bank of China">Exim Bank of China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Urgewald_2018_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Urgewald_2018-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Bank_for_International_Cooperation" title="Japan Bank for International Cooperation">Japan Bank for International Cooperation</a> and Indian public sector banks.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kazakhstan#Coal" title="Energy in Kazakhstan">Coal in Kazakhstan</a> was the main recipient of coal consumption subsidies totalling US$2 billion in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coal_in_Turkey#Subsidies" title="Coal in Turkey">Coal in Turkey</a> benefited from substantial subsidies.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stranded_assets">Stranded assets</span></h3>
<p>Some coal-fired power stations could become <a href="/wiki/Stranded_assets" class="mw-redirect" title="Stranded assets">stranded assets</a>, for example <a href="/wiki/China_Energy_Investment" title="China Energy Investment">China Energy Investment</a>, the world's largest power company, risks losing half its capital.<sup id="cite_ref-CarbTrk2018_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarbTrk2018-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> However state owned electricity utilities such as <a href="/wiki/Eskom" title="Eskom">Eskom</a> in South Africa, <a href="/wiki/Perusahaan_Listrik_Negara" title="Perusahaan Listrik Negara">Perusahaan Listrik Negara</a> in Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Sarawak_Energy" title="Sarawak Energy">Sarawak Energy</a> in Malaysia, <a href="/wiki/Taipower" class="mw-redirect" title="Taipower">Taipower</a> in Taiwan, <a href="/wiki/EGAT" class="mw-redirect" title="EGAT">EGAT</a> in Thailand, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_Electricity" title="Vietnam Electricity">Vietnam Electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/E%C3%9CA%C5%9E" class="mw-redirect" title="EÜAŞ">EÜAŞ</a> in Turkey are building or planning new plants.<sup id="cite_ref-Urgewald_2018_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Urgewald_2018-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Coal&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> this may be helping to cause a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_bubble" title="Carbon bubble">carbon bubble</a> which could cause financial instability if it bursts.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<p>Countries building or financing new coal-fired power stations, such as Japan, face mounting international criticism for obstructing the aims of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornot-Gandolfe_2018_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornot-Gandolfe_2018-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> And Australia is being criticised by the Pacific Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian2018_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2018-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span></h3>
<p>Allegations of corruption are being investigated in India<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and China.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_coal">Opposition to coal</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_(25563929593).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg/220px-Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg/330px-Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg/440px-Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_(25563929593).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesting damage to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a> caused by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Australia" title="Climate change in Australia">climate change in Australia</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gemeinsam_stark,Hambacher_Forst,NRW.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg/220px-Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg/330px-Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg/440px-Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gemeinsam_stark,Hambacher_Forst,NRW.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tree houses for protesting the felling of part of <a href="/wiki/Hambach_Forest" title="Hambach Forest">Hambach Forest</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Hambach_surface_mine" title="Hambach surface mine">Hambach surface mine</a> in Germany: after which the felling was suspended in 2018</div></div></div>
<p>Opposition to coal pollution was one of the main reasons the modern <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmental movement</a> started in the 19th century.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_away_from_coal">Transition away from coal</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_phase-out#Coal" title="Fossil fuel phase-out">Fossil fuel phase-out §&#160;Coal</a></div>
<p>In order to meet global climate goals and provide power to those that don't currently have it coal power must be reduced from nearly 10,000 TWh to less than 2,000 TWh by 2040.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Many countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Powering_Past_Coal_Alliance" title="Powering Past Coal Alliance">Powering Past Coal Alliance</a>, have already or are transitioned away from coal;<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> the largest transition announced so far being Germany, which is due to shut down its last coal-fired power station between 2035 and 2038.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Some countries use the ideas of a "just transition", for example to use some of the benefits of transition to provide early pensions for coal miners.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> However low-lying <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a> are concerned the transition is not fast enough and that they will be inundated by <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>; so they have called for <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries to completely phase out coal by 2030 and other countries by 2040.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian2018_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2018-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peak_coal">Peak coal</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg/220px-Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg/330px-Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg/440px-Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A coal mine in <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, United States. The United States has the world's largest coal reserves.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Peak_coal" title="Peak coal">Peak coal</a></div>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Coal_by_country" title="Coal by country">many countries have coal</a> underground not all will be consumed.
</p><p>Of the three fossil fuels, coal has the most widely distributed resources. Coal is mined on all continents except Antarctica. However many such resources have no economic value (much value has been destroyed by shale gas fracking).<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The largest resources are found in the United States, Russia, China, Australia and India:
</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto; text-align:right;">

<p>Nowadays "peak coal" means the point in time when consumption of coal reaches a maximum. As of 2018 global peak coal consumption is predicted to occur by the early 2020s at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-IDDRI_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDDRI-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switch_to_cleaner_fuels_and_lower_carbon_electricity_generation">Switch to cleaner fuels and lower carbon electricity generation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas#Power_generation" title="Natural gas">Natural gas §&#160;Power generation</a></div>
<p>Coal-fired generation puts out about twice the amount of carbon dioxide—around a tonne for every megawatt hour generated—than electricity generated by burning natural gas at 500&#160;kg of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> per megawatt hour.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In addition to generating electricity, natural gas is also popular in some countries for heating and as an <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle" title="Natural gas vehicle">automotive fuel</a>.
</p><p>The use of <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Energy in the United Kingdom">coal in the United Kingdom</a> declined as a result of the development of <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_oil" title="North Sea oil">North Sea oil</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Dash_for_gas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dash for gas">dash for gas</a> during the 1990s. In Canada some <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">coal power plants</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hearn_Generating_Station" title="Hearn Generating Station">Hearn Generating Station</a>, switched from coal to natural gas. In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_in_the_United_States" title="Coal power in the United States">coal power in the United States</a> provided 30% of the electricity, down from approximately 49% in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTKentucky_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTKentucky-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> due to plentiful supplies of low cost natural gas obtained by <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">hydraulic fracturing</a> of tight shale formations.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTKentucky_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTKentucky-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coal_regions_in_transition">Coal regions in transition</span></h3>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Coal-mining_region" title="Coal-mining region">coal-mining regions</a> are highly dependent on coal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span></h3>
<p>Some coal miners are concerned their jobs may be lost in the transition.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bioremediation">Bioremediation</span></h3>
<p>The white rot fungus <i><a href="/wiki/Trametes_versicolor" title="Trametes versicolor">Trametes versicolor</a></i> can grow on and metabolize naturally occurring coal.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The bacteria <a href="/wiki/Diplococcus" title="Diplococcus">Diplococcus</a> has been found to degrade coal, raising its temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_usage">Cultural usage</span></h2>
<p>Coal is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_minerals,_rocks,_stones_and_gemstones" title="List of U.S. state minerals, rocks, stones and gemstones">official state mineral</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and the official state rock of <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> both <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a> have a historic link to coal mining.
</p><p>Some cultures hold that children who misbehave will receive only a lump of coal from <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a> for Christmas in their <a href="/wiki/Christmas_stocking" title="Christmas stocking">christmas stockings</a> instead of presents.
</p><p>It is also customary and considered lucky in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="North of England">North of England</a> to give coal as a gift on <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year&#39;s Day">New Year's Day</a>. This occurs as part of <a href="/wiki/First-Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="First-Foot">First-Footing</a> and represents warmth for the year to come.
</p>
